[1:1:344,387] coordinates transportation policies and programs  

[1:2:344,397] to achieve the state's mobility, safety, and  

[1:3:344,407] environmental sustainability objectives. The

[1:5:344,427] the following state entities: Department of  

[1:6:344,437] Transportation, California Transportation  

[1:7:344,447] Commission, High-Speed Rail Authority,  

[1:8:344,457] Department of Motor Vehicles, California Highway  

[1:9:344,466] Patrol, and the Board of Pilot Commissioners.

[1:0:178,53] 2600   California Transportation Commission  

[1:1:66,75] The California Transportation Commission is responsible for programming and allocating funds for the construction and  

[1:2:66,85] improvement of highways, passenger rail systems, and transit systems throughout California. The Commission advises and  

[1:3:66,95] assists the Transportation Agency and the Legislature in formulating and evaluating state policies and plans for California's  

[1:4:66,105] transportation programs. The Commission also initiates and develops state and federal transportation policies that seek to  

[1:5:66,116] secure financial stability for the state.

[5:0:66,269] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,289] 1800 - ADMINISTRATION OF THE CALIFORNIA TRANSPORTATION COMMISSION  

[6:0:66,309] This program reviews and adopts the State Transportation Improvement Program, the State Highway Operation and Protection  

[6:1:66,319] Program, the Active Transportation Program, the Local Partnership program, the Solutions for Congested Corridors Program,  

[6:2:66,330] the Trade Corridor Enhancement Program, and adopts the State Transportation Improvement Program Fund Estimate. The  

[6:3:66,340] program also approves city and county eligibility for a portion of the funding in the Local Streets and Roads Program.  

[6:4:66,350] Additionally, the program allocates transportation revenues and bond funds for highways, passenger rail systems, active  

[6:5:66,360] transportation, and transit system improvements in California. The program also collaborates with and provides guidance to  

[6:6:66,370] other state and local transportation agencies on a variety of transportation issues including planning, asset management, and  

[6:7:66,381] system improvements.  

[6:8:66,398] 1805 - CLEAN AIR AND TRANSPORTATION IMPROVEMENT  

[7:0:66,419] This program allocates Proposition 116 bond funds to the Department of Transportation, the Department of Parks and  

[7:1:66,429] Recreation, and local agencies that are used for the preservation, acquisition, construction, and improvement of rail  

[7:2:66,439] infrastructure, paratransit vehicles, bicycle facilities, water-borne ferry vessels and facilities, public transit, and the California  

[7:3:66,449] State Museum of Railroad Technology.

[5:0:66,398] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,418] 1830019 - AERONAUTICS  

[6:0:66,438] The Aeronautics Program supports California's aviation activities by promoting the safe and effective use of airports and  

[6:1:66,448] heliports. This program oversees safety compliance and provides engineering and financial assistance for safety and  

[6:2:66,458] infrastructure improvements. The division maintains the California Aviation System Plan, provides guidance for land use  

[6:3:66,469] compatibility in areas around airports, administers airport noise standards and regulations, and enhances goods movement to  

[6:4:66,479] and from airports through improved ground access.  

[6:5:66,496] 1835010 - CAPITAL OUTLAY SUPPORT  

[7:0:66,514] The Capital Outlay Support Program is responsible for developing capital projects on the state highway system and preparing  

[7:1:66,524] these for the construction phase. Functions of this program include the activities necessary to deliver construction projects,  

[7:2:66,535] such as engineering and design work, environmental studies, right-of-way acquisition, and construction inspection activities.  

[7:3:66,545] The program also oversees private contractors that undertake the direct construction work for projects.  

[7:4:66,562] 1835019 - CAPITAL OUTLAY PROJECTS  

[8:0:66,580] The Capital Outlay Projects Program funds capacity projects in the State Transportation Improvement Program and repair  

[8:1:66,590] projects in the State Highway Operations and Protection Program. Projects are programmed by Caltrans and funding is  

[8:2:66,601] allocated by the California Transportation Commission. Project funding is used for acquisition of right-of-way and for  

[8:3:66,611] construction.  

[8:4:66,628] 1835020 - LOCAL ASSISTANCE  

[9:0:66,646] The Local Assistance Program provides state and federal funds to over 600 cities, counties and regional agencies to improve  

[9:1:66,656] their transportation infrastructure or provide transportation services. The program also provides guidance, expertise, and  

[9:2:66,667] oversight of transportation projects to monitor compliance with state and federal requirements to ensure successful project  

[9:3:66,677] completion.  

[9:4:66,694] 1835029 - PROGRAM DEVELOPMENT  

[10:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

# === PAGE 13 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] TRANSPORTATION 

[1:0:413,13] 2020-21 STATE BUDGET — TRN   11 

[2:0:168,29] 2660   Department of Transportation - Continued 

[3:0:66,83] The Program Development Program assists the department in fully utilizing available state and federal transportation funds for  

[3:1:66,93] both the state highway and intercity rail systems. The Division of Research, Innovation and System Information provides  

[3:2:66,103] research and data solutions needed to make informed decisions that improve California's transportation system. The Division  

[3:3:66,113] of Transportation Programming produces the State Transportation Improvement Program, State Highway Operations and  

[3:4:66,124] Protection Program, and the Federal Statewide Transportation Improvement Program documents.  

[4:0:66,141] 1835038 - LEGAL  

[5:0:66,159] The Legal Program advises the department on federal and state statutes, regulations, and case law, and how those laws  

[5:1:66,169] impact Caltrans' policy makers, operational needs, and associated risks. Through the Legal program, Caltrans handles all of its  

[5:2:66,179] own legal affairs, including: real property acquisition and management, construction, environmental, personnel, tort litigation,  

[5:3:66,190] and other matters. The program handles over 1,400 active legal matters, issues, and litigation cases annually. The program  

[5:4:66,200] also provides the High Speed Rail Authority fully reimbursed eminent domain legal services.  

[6:0:66,218] 1835047 - OPERATIONS  

[7:0:66,235] The Operations Program establishes statewide policies and procedures related to traffic management, identifies and prioritizes  

[7:1:66,245] the programming of highway safety and operational improvement projects, and manages the Statewide Transportation and  

[7:2:66,256] Encroachment Permits programs. The program also supports efficient system operation by administering incident management  

[7:3:66,266] and traveler information programs, providing technical support to local agencies, responding to incidents on state highways,  

[7:4:66,276] and providing traffic design support for design engineers.  

[8:0:66,294] 1835056 - MAINTENANCE  

[9:0:66,311] The Maintenance Program preserves California's highways by maintaining and repairing the state highway system. The  

[9:1:66,322] program achieves its objectives through a fix-it first approach, including: (1) preventive and corrective pavement maintenance;  

[9:2:66,332] (2) bridge inspection, load rating, and maintenance; (3) culvert inspection and maintenance; and (4) maintenance and repair of  

[9:3:66,342] traffic management system field elements. In addition, the program strives to improve highway travel, safety, and the  

[9:4:66,352] environment through testing, research, and technology development.  

[10:0:66,370] 1840019 - STATE AND FEDERAL MASS TRANSIT  

[11:0:66,388] The State and Federal Mass Transit Program administers state and federal grants that provide funding for operating  

[11:1:66,398] assistance, capital improvements, and equipment to public transportation agencies. The program assists agencies with  

[11:2:66,408] purchasing buses, rolling stock, and ferries; supports commuter and urban rail services and waterborne ferry operations; and  

[11:3:66,418] assists in providing services accessible to the elderly and disabled. The program achieves its objectives through: (1)  

[11:4:66,428] management of state and federal capital and operations grant programs; (2) planning, support, and coordination of mass  

[11:5:66,439] transportation services; and (3) administering state bond programs and state funding that directly support public transportation  

[11:6:66,449] efforts.  

[12:0:66,467] 1840028 - INTERCITY RAIL PASSENGER PROGRAM  

[13:0:66,484] The Intercity Rail Passenger Program helps to reduce highway congestion and automobile fuel consumption while improving  

[13:1:66,494] air quality and environmental protection by providing leadership in the planning and implementation of a passenger rail  

[13:2:66,505] transportation system. The program achieves its objectives through the: (1) support and funding of the intercity rail lines  

[13:3:66,515] administered by the Joint Powers Authorities; (2) management of state and federal rail capital improvement programs; (3)  

[13:4:66,525] ownership of state passenger rail equipment; and (4) development of the California State Rail Plan.  

[14:0:66,543] 1845013 - STATEWIDE PLANNING  

[15:0:66,560] The Statewide Planning Program implements statewide transportation policy through coordinated planning at the federal, state,  

[15:1:66,571] regional, and local levels. The program prepares the long-range state transportation plan, provides long-range interregional  

[15:2:66,581] transportation system planning and transportation planning studies to inform the State Transportation Improvement Program,  

[15:3:66,591] and supports departmental policies and programs such as goods movement and climate action. The program also prepares the  

[15:4:66,601] Interregional Transportation Strategic Plan, which guides investment of the Interregional Improvement Program funds in the  

[15:5:66,611] State Transportation Improvement Program.  

[16:0:66,629] 1845022 - REGIONAL PLANNING  

[17:0:66,647] The Regional Planning Program implements statewide transportation policy through coordination at the regional level and  

[17:1:66,657] develops transportation plans and projects. The program develops long-range regional transportation plans and provides long-

[17:2:66,667] range transportation system analysis and transportation planning studies as input to regional transportation plans. The program  

[17:3:66,677] also prepares transportation planning studies to support Caltrans policies and programs such as air quality and smart mobility.  

[18:0:66,695] 1850010 - EQUIPMENT SERVICE PROGRAM  

[19:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,83] The Equipment Service Program provides mobile fleet equipment and services to other departmental programs through: (1)  

[3:1:66,93] purchasing fleet equipment and related components, (2) receiving, servicing, and equipping new units, (3) managing the fleet,  

[3:2:66,103] (4) repairing and maintaining the fleet, including payments for fuel and insurance, and (5) disposing of end-of-life fleet assets.  

[3:3:66,121] 1870 - OFFICE OF INSPECTOR GENERAL  

[4:0:66,139] The Office of Inspector General Program delivers professional audits and investigative services that assist management in  

[4:1:66,149] accomplishing departmental goals and objectives, setting priorities and making efficient, effective, and financially responsible  

[4:2:66,159] transportation decisions, Additionally, the office informs the Director, the Secretary of Transportation, the Legislature, and the  

[4:3:66,169] California Transportation Commission on issues concerning fraud, improper activities or other serious abuses or deficiencies  

[4:4:66,179] relating to the expenditure of transportation funds or administration of Department programs and operations. Major activities  

[4:5:66,190] include audits of external entities, internal performance audits and investigations.  

[4:6:66,207] 9900100 - ADMINISTRATION  

[5:0:66,225] The Administration Program supports the operations of the department. Major activities include accounting, budgeting, office  

[5:1:66,235] facility operations and management, information technology, human resources, procurement and contracting, training,  

[5:2:66,245] workforce planning, and labor relations.

[10:0:68,587] 2670   Board of Pilot Commissioners for the Bays of San Francisco, San Pablo, and  

[10:1:285,601] Suisun  

[11:0:66,623] The Board of Pilot Commissioners for the Bays of San Francisco, San Pablo, and Suisun is the oversight body that licenses  

[11:1:66,633] and regulates the maritime pilots who navigate certain large vessels entering or leaving those bays, Monterey Bay, and on  

[11:2:66,643] tributaries to Sacramento and Stockton.  

[12:0:66,663] The Board's responsibilities include training and licensing maritime pilots, establishing standards for pilot fitness, incident  

[12:1:66,674] investigation, approval of pilot boat acquisitions and improvements, oversight of the San Francisco Bar Pilot Pension Plan, and  

[12:2:66,684] providing pilotage fee rate recommendations to the Legislature. The seven members of the Board are appointed by the  

[12:3:66,694] Governor with the consent of the Senate, and the Secretary of the Transportation Agency is an ex-officio member. The Board  

[12:4:66,704] was established in California's first Legislative Session, and has been in continuous existence since 1850.  

[13:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

# === PAGE 57 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] TRANSPORTATION 

[1:0:412,13] 2020-21 STATE BUDGET — TRN   55 

[2:0:68,29] 2670   Board of Pilot Commissioners for the Bays of San Francisco, San Pablo, and 

[3:0:66,83] All of the operational and program expenses of the Board are funded by various surcharges set by the Board, and are paid by  

[3:1:66,93] the shipping companies that utilize services of Board-licensed maritime pilots. The Board Operations Surcharge funds the cost  

[3:2:66,103] of Board operations, and is set as a percentage of pilotage fees. Three separate surcharges are based upon ship movements  

[3:3:66,113] and fund a continuing education program for pilots, a pilot trainee training program, and the acquisition of navigation technology  

[3:4:66,124] for use by pilots. Two separate surcharges are based on the tonnage of the vessel that arrives or leaves the San Francisco Bay  

[3:5:66,134] and fund pilot boat acquisitions and improvements, and the San Francisco Bar Pilot Pension Plan.

[4:0:66,470] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:1:66,489] 2050 - TRAFFIC MANAGEMENT  

[5:0:66,509] The objectives of this program are to minimize deaths, injuries, and property losses due to traffic accidents; to reduce traffic  

[5:1:66,520] delays to the motoring public; to provide protection and assistance to the motoring public, state employees and property,  

[5:2:66,530] including protection of the State Capitol and the surrounding grounds, state constitutional officers, and visiting dignitaries; and  

[5:3:66,540] to curtail the potential for terrorist threats as part of broader state and federal homeland security efforts. These objectives are  

[5:4:66,550] achieved through both ground and flight operations.  

[5:5:66,568] 2055 - REGULATION AND INSPECTION  

[6:0:66,586] The CHP operates 55 commercial vehicle enforcement facilities statewide with the objectives of:  

[6:1:65,603] • Reducing the incidence of truck and bus accidents attributable to defective vehicle equipment, improper maintenance,  

[6:2:76,613] loading or securing of cargo, or disqualified drivers.  

[7:0:65,630] • Protecting the public from spills of hazardous materials or specially regulated loads, and from the improper operation of  

[7:1:76,640] specified vehicles such as ambulances and armored cars.  

[8:0:65,656] • Protecting farm workers transported in farm labor vehicles and children transported in school buses.  

[8:1:65,672] • Ensuring that proper registration fees are paid, and protecting highways from excessive vehicle weights.

[8:3:66,708] This program protects the public from vehicle theft through:

[12:1:66,646] and/or identification cards to those who meet specific criteria, provides information from driver license and identification card  

[12:2:66,657] records to state and local law enforcement agencies, and collects voter registration information.

[13:1:66,705] operating on public roadways.
